<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?What is Property?> "The French <a href="Pierre-Joseph%20Proudhon">Pierre-Joseph Proudhon</a> is regarded as the first self-proclaimed anarchist, a label he adopted in his groundbreaking work "What is Property?", published in 1840." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?spontaneous order> " He developed the theory of spontaneous order in society, where organisation emerges without a central coordinator imposing its own idea of order against the wills of individuals acting in their own interests." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?Property is theft> " In "What is Property?", Proudhon answers with the famous accusation "Property is theft"." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?capitalist> " His opposition to the state, organised religion and certain capitalist practices inspired subsequent anarchists and made him one of the leading social thinkers of his time." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?anarcho-communist> "The anarcho-communist <a href="Joseph%20D%C3%A9jacque">Joseph Déjacque</a> was the first person to describe himself as "<a href="Libertarianism">libertarian</a>"." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?Joseph Déjacque> "The <a href="Anarcho-communism">anarcho-communist</a> Joseph Déjacque was the first person to describe himself as "<a href="Libertarianism">libertarian</a>"." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?libertarian> " Since the 1890s and beginning in France, the term "<a href="libertarianism">libertarianism</a>" has often been used as a synonym for anarchism and was used almost exclusively in this sense until the 1950s in the United States, though its use as a synonym is still common outside the United States." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?Max Stirner> " In 1844, the post-hegelian philosopher Max Stirner published in Germany the book, "<a href="The%20Ego%20and%20Its%20Own">The Ego and Its Own</a>", which would later be considered an influential early text of <a href="individualist%20anarchism">individualist anarchism</a>." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?The Ego and Its Own> " In 1844, the post-hegelian philosopher <a href="Max%20Stirner">Max Stirner</a> published in Germany the book, "The Ego and Its Own", which would later be considered an influential early text of <a href="individualist%20anarchism">individualist anarchism</a>."

<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?targeted killings> " Scholars such as Beverly Gage contend that this was not advocacy of mass murder, but targeted killings of members of the <a href="ruling%20class">ruling class</a> at times when such actions might garner sympathy from the population, such as during periods of heightened government repression or labor conflicts where workers were killed."

<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=12> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?direct democracy> "<a href="Anarcho-communism">Anarcho-communism</a> (also known as anarchist-communism, libertarian communism and occasionally as free communism) is a theory of anarchism that advocates abolition of the state, <a href="market%20%28economics%29">market</a>s, money, <a href="private%20property">private property</a> (while retaining respect for personal property) and capitalism in favour of <a href="common%20ownership">common ownership</a> of the <a href="means%20of%20production">means of production</a>, direct democracy and a horizontal network of <a href="voluntary%20association">voluntary association</a>s and <a href="workers%27%20council">workers' council</a>s with production and consumption based on the guiding principle: "<a href="From%20each%20according%20to%20his%20ability%2C%20to%20each%20according%20to%20his%20needs">From each according to his ability, to each according to his need</a>"."

<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?inhibition> "The second category focuses on nonsocial or general processing: the <a href="executive%20functions">executive functions</a> such as <a href="working%20memory">working memory</a>, planning, inhibition." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?executive dysfunction> " In his review, Kenworthy states that "the claim of executive dysfunction as a causal factor in autism is controversial", however, "it is clear that executive dysfunction plays a role in the social and cognitive deficits observed in individuals with autism"." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?Weak central coherence theory> "Weak central coherence theory hypothesizes that a limited ability to see the big picture underlies the central disturbance in autism." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?perceptual> " A related theory—enhanced perceptual functioning—focuses more on the superiority of locally oriented and perceptual operations in autistic individuals." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?monotropism> " Yet another, monotropism, posits that autism stems from a different cognitive style, tending to focus attention (or processing resources) intensely, to the exclusion of other stimuli."

<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?psychosocial> " Although many psychosocial interventions have some positive evidence, suggesting that some form of treatment is preferable to no treatment, the methodological quality of <a href="systematic%20review">systematic review</a>s of these studies has generally been poor, their clinical results are mostly tentative, and there is little evidence for the relative effectiveness of treatment options." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=25> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?systematic review> " Although many <a href="psychosocial">psychosocial</a> interventions have some positive evidence, suggesting that some form of treatment is preferable to no treatment, the methodological quality of systematic reviews of these studies has generally been poor, their clinical results are mostly tentative, and there is little evidence for the relative effectiveness of treatment options."

<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=39> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?Aerosols> "Aerosols (very fine particles/droplets in the atmosphere) have both direct and indirect effects on Earth's radiative balance." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=39> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?cloud condensation nuclei> " The direct (albedo) effect is generally to cool the planet; the indirect effect (the particles act as cloud condensation nuclei and thereby change cloud properties) is less certain." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=39> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?black carbon> " As per the effects are:Another albedo-related effect on the climate is from black carbon particles." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=39> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change> " The size of this effect is difficult to quantify: the Intergovernmental Panel on Climate Change estimates that the global mean radiative forcing for black carbon aerosols from fossil fuels is +0." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=39> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?Single-scattering albedo> "Single-scattering albedo is used to define scattering of electromagnetic waves on small particles." 
<https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?curid=39> <https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki?refractive index> " It depends on properties of the material (refractive index); the size of the particle or particles; and the wavelength of the incoming radiation."
